  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7bf10b41-4e1f-46c9-9508-f1f831c69800'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText1540888141653949414" style="display:none"><i>These violent delights have violent ends<br />And in their triumph die, like fire and powder,<br />Which as they kiss consume.<br />-William Shakespeare,</i><br />ROMEO AND JULIET<br /><br />Juliet Capulet didn't take her own life. She was murdered by the person she trusted most, her new husband, Romeo Montague, who made the sacrifice to ensure his own immortality. But Romeo didn't anticipate that Juliet would be granted eternal life as well, and would become an agent for the Ambassadors of Light.<br /><br />For seven hundred years, Juliet has struggled to preserve romantic love and the lives of the innocent, while Romeo has fought for the dark side, seeking to destroy the human heart. Until now.<br /><br />Now Juliet has found her own forbidden love, and Romeo, O Romeo, will do everything in his power to destroy their happiness.<br /><br />Secrets unfold and surprises abound in Stacey Jay's powerfully dark romance, which reunites literature's most tragic couple.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944721559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7361380658647467378"><blockquote>
  <i>I’ll have to decide: join Romeo or let the specter of my soul take me. I know I should be afraid for my future, but all I can think about is Ben.</i>
</blockquote><b>This book mocks the original Juliet's weakness, only to have the newly improved Juliet just as fucking dumb as the original.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400815858i/9724718._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So the original Shakespeare version, Juliet met Romeo, fell in love, and died for love within three days. In this retelling of Juliet's story, before this book starts, Juliet still ran away with Romeo, and then said Romeo stabb</span>
  <span id="freeText7361380658647467378" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I’ll have to decide: join Romeo or let the specter of my soul take me. I know I should be afraid for my future, but all I can think about is Ben.</i>
</blockquote><b>This book mocks the original Juliet's weakness, only to have the newly improved Juliet just as fucking dumb as the original.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400815858i/9724718._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So the original Shakespeare version, Juliet met Romeo, fell in love, and died for love within three days. In this retelling of Juliet's story, before this book starts, Juliet still ran away with Romeo, and then said Romeo stabbed her and ate her like a zombie. Flesh and blood dripping from his mouth and everything. It was pretty neat.<br><br>Flash forward 700 years in which Juliet is older, wiser, more wary of <b>the perils of insta-love</b>? Fucking nope!<br><br>One would think a reimagined, powerful, supernatural Juliet would have learned a fucking lesson or two: nope!<br><br>This book was terrible. Here is why:<br><br>- <b>A stupid, stupid main character</b> who makes the same mistake as the original Juliet, made worse by the fact that she was KILLED the first time. She's ruled by her passions, there is no reason in her behavior.<br><br>- <b>Insta-love</b>, a <b>love triangle</b> between the new, improved <b>zombie Romeo</b> and new boy <b>Ben Luna</b>. Ben. Ben. GEE, I WONDER WHO BEN COULD BE?! It's not like he has a character with a similar name in <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> or anything!!!11<br><br>- <b>Terrible side characters</b>: basically, the stars of the book are Juliet and Ben. Nobody else need apply.<br><br>- <b>Poor setting</b>: The whole we're gonna give you renewed life so you can play Cupid? No.<br><br>- <b>Poor female characters</b>: Her best friend, her "mother," both uncaring, cruel, callous bitches, depicted as inferior to Juliet (insta-love Juliet) in every way.<br><br>- <b>The premise</b>: weak as Ben and Juliet's insta-love. The idea of a love ambassador is pretty bloody and neat until you take into consideration the fact that it doesn't make any sense at all, and I'm not talking about the suspension of disbelief and the supernatural element. I'm talking about the fact that the reasoning behind the soul mate thing makes no fucking sense.<br><br><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>He turns and our eyes meet, and that sense of knowing him hits, catching me in my empty gut. For a moment, the sadness and pain in his eyes is my pain, and I desperately want to make it better. I want to reach for him, hold him, whisper into the warm crook of his neck that everything is going to be okay, that I’ll make it that way.</i>
</blockquote>(Psst, that's the first time they meet)<br><br><b>Day 0.5</b> (because it takes place when the day's practically over):<br><br>Juliet is awake! Well, kind of. This ain't Shakespeare's Juliet...well, she's the inspiration for it, but the Shakespearean version was a falsehood, told to the dude by the sneaky, conniving son of a bitch that's Romeo. The real Juliet died at age 14, in 1304 Verona. Killed by the man she loved. And now Romeo is kind of a zombie. He reincarnates from one life to another, living constantly on earth as an immortal <b>Mercenary</b>, whereas Juliet only gets to come back to earth once in awhile, as an <b>Ambassador.</b> Think of her as <b>Cupid</b>, she makes sure that a pair of true lovers end up together, or else they will fall prey to the forces of darkness and one of them will die a horrible death like she did. At the hands of Romeo. Did I say that Romeo is a zombie? He's a total zombie.<blockquote>
  <i>...flesh in his teeth, blood dripping down his chin.</i>
</blockquote>So now Juliet has been given an assignment, she's given the body of <b>Ariel Dragland</b>, a <b>stunningly beautiful, extremely thin platinum-blonde high school outcast</b> with self-esteem issues and mommy problems. Yeah, an outcast, because she's a little bit scarred from being burned as a child.<br><br>So here's Juliet/Ariel. On earth. Almost dead from a car accident, and OH CRAP THERE'S ROMEO, now in the body of a boy named <b>Dylan</b>. Juliet/Ariel runs like fuck, Romeo is chasing after her (he's a fast zombie), and OMG YAY A CAR. She runs into the car, and is <b>struck down by insta-love</b>. The rescuer is a high school boy named <b>Ben Luna.</b> The attraction is immediate.<blockquote>
  <i>I’m suddenly very aware of him, as well, of his front warming my back, his thighs shifting beneath mine. I clear my throat, blushing for the first time in so long the strangeness of hot cheeks makes me blink.</i>
</blockquote>Ben is Mexican-American. He likes to uses randomly inserted Spanish words.<blockquote>
  <i>“Then this really isn’t your lucky night, chica."</i>
</blockquote>I almost typed "Mexican words" for a moment before I caught myself. Lol. We all have our brain farts.<br><br>So crazy zombie Romeo/Dylan is after Ariel/Juliet. They go to the same high school. Hooray! Doesn't matter. What's important is BEN. BEN. She feels such...familiarity with him, she feels an intense longing for him, despite <b>knowing Ben that night for all of 1 hour.</b>She wants to kiss him as he drops her off.<blockquote>
  <i>I stay and let him come closer, closer, until I can feel the heat of his lips and imagine just how perfect they’ll feel, how perfect he’ll taste, how—</i>
</blockquote>She can't stop thinking about him for the rest of the night.<blockquote>
  <i>I fist the damp wipe in my hand, reining in the part of me that aches for this boy with the big brown eyes.<br>I might feel an instant connection to Ben, but I don’t matter.</i>
</blockquote>Famous last words.<br><br>Ben is Mexican.<blockquote>
  <i>"Dulces sueños, Mermaid.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Day 2</b>: So Juliet's still got a job to do, right? She's got to <b>find the designated couple of soulmates and make them fall in love</b> or else one of them will die a horrible horrible death. Nobody wants that, except for Romeo. Awesome. So where are they? As it turned out, one of the couple is <b>Gemma</b>, Juliet/Ariel's best friend <b>since second grade.</b> The one girl who has befriended Ariel despite the entire class neglecting and making fun of her. There's an aura over her head. <b>Gemma is 1/2 of the soulmate.</b><blockquote>
  <i>And then I turn back to Gemma...lost in the rosy glow surrounding her chest.</i>
</blockquote>And <b>the other 1/2 of the soulmates?</b><blockquote>
  <i><b>Ben.</b> Something in my gut twists and for a moment I’m dizzy, weightless, as if the floor has been ripped from beneath me, but I don’t know which way to fall.</i>
</blockquote>Well, awesome! Best friend in love and designated to be soulmates with the guy who saved her the other night. What could be better? <b>Well, for starters, JULIET CAN'T STOP THINKING ABOUT BEN.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I shake my head. This has to stop. I can’t go to pieces every time I see his face. I have to pull it together, be a good influence, make sure he commits to the love of his life and lives happily ever after.</i>
</blockquote>But it doesn't. Juliet can't stop thinking about him. Romeo is on her ass. And <b>Ben is still determined to prove to us that he's Mexican.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Ben laughs. “Dios mio. Fine, crazy woman.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Day 3</b>: GEMMA. THAT BITCH. SHE'S SO NOT WORTHY OF BEN. I'M NOT GOING TO GIVE HER TO BEN.<blockquote>
  <i>Gemma’s thoughtless at best, mean-spirited and selfish at worst, and I want so much better for Ben.</i>
</blockquote>What?! Where the fuck did that come from?! Ok, so Juliet's in love with Ben. Romeo's still there declaring his undying (that was a zombie joke) love for Juliet if only she'd give him another chance. And Ben? <b>After three (ok, 2.2?) days of knowing her, this is how he feels.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m not doing this right, and I know I sound crazy, but...I love you. I could see myself loving you for a long time.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Well, that escalated quickly.</b> Three days. Three motherfucking days.<blockquote>
  <i>“I love you. I want to do everything with you. I want to marry you and have kids with you and get old with you. And then I want to die the day before you do, so I never have to live without you.”</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400815858i/9724719._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NOOOOOOOOOOO. WHYYYYYYYYYYYY. <b>Do your fucking job, Juliet.</b> Need I remind you of what would happen if you don't unite the soulmates?<blockquote>
  <i>These two are my job, and if I don’t do it, one of them will die. Either they commit to each other or one of them commits murder and becomes a Mercenary. That’s the way it goes. Every. Single. Time.</i>
</blockquote><b>Fuck you, Juliet, you stupid bitch.</b> YOU HAD ONE JOB.<br><br>Ben is still Mexican.<blockquote>
  <i>“Dios mio,” Ben says.</i>
</blockquote><u>Juliet</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>How can I think of loving someone again? How have I let this happen? Even if it weren’t forbidden, haven’t I learned my lesson?</i>
</blockquote><b>Apparently not</b>. Juliet is a motherfucking moron. She's techniaclly over 700 years old, but she hasn't spent all that time on Earth.<blockquote>
  <i>I’ve seen centuries pass, but I died when I was fourteen and have spent less than twenty conscious years on earth.</i>
</blockquote>20 years. That's a long time as an adult. Time spent being Cupid, making soulmates meet. <b>She's been betrayed by love. She's seen the harm love can do. She knows the consequences of destined soulmates NOT falling in love, and she doesn't learn a motherfucking thing.</b> She fell into insta-love with Romeo and elopes. He kills her. One would think she would know better not to fall into insta-love again. After THREE MOTHERFUCKING DAYS. She knows that the soulmates who aren't together will end up in a horrible death. SHE IGNORES THAT FOR HER OWN MOTHERFUCKING INSTA-LOVE. Gemma doesn't deserve him, says <b>Juliet, the worst fucking Cupid ever.</b><br><br>Not only that, she's determined to destroy the only friendship thar her borrowed body, Ariel, has. Gemma is her only friend. Ariel suffers from crippling shyness. Ariel has no other friends. And yet Juliet as Ariel <b>sees fit to steal away her best friend's soulmate.</b><blockquote>
  <i>She and Gemma are so different. It’s amazing they’ve stayed friends for as long as they have.<br>But they have, and it doesn’t matter what I think. I can’t let Ariel lose this friendship. I could be gone by the end of the day.</i>
</blockquote><b>That would be such a fucking cute sentiment if Juliet didn't steal away Ben under poor Gemma's nose.</b><br><br>Oh my god, the love. THE LOVE. <b>Juliet is so fucking purple-prosey-lovey-dovey.</b> She can't contain her fucking emotions for Ben, a boy whom, I don't know if I've mentioned this before, but SHE'S KNOWN HIM FOR LESS THAN THREE DAYS. By the end of day 2, she's ready to declare her love. It's pure insta-love. There is no emotion behind it. She feels the familiarity, the desire, that's it. One little word from him is like AAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAAHHH MOTHERFUCKING CHERUBS SINGING FROM HEAVEN. <b>Juliet is easily impressed.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Romeo might have praised my loveliness with lyrical poetry, but he never made me feel as beautiful as Ben did when he said four simple words.<br>You matter to me.</i>
</blockquote>Puh-please. Is that all it takes to get her to drop her panties? Be a little better than that. Have more fucking depths than that. Am I to believe that Juliet is a motherfucking <b>Immortal Warrior?</b> Fucking no.<br><br><u>The Girl Hate</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>"You’re the one who messed up when you got pregnant when you were nineteen."</i>
</blockquote><b>Way to be a bitch to your own mother.</b> Well, to Ariel's mother, but it's Ariel who's going to have to live with the consequences.<br><br><b>This book hates women.</b> Juliet/Ariel's mother is a careless person. Unfeeling about her daughter's feelings. Terrible at showing her love, even if Juliet acknowledges that she does love her daughter.<blockquote>
  <i>She means that she cares, no matter how bad she is at showing it.</i>
</blockquote>Her best friend <b>Gemma</b>, is also <b>another careless person.</b><blockquote>
  <i>The hard light in Gemma’s eyes fades, and for a second I can see that she cares. Or that she wants to care.</i>
</blockquote>So none of the female side characters in this book is careing and loving and nice at all. To be fair, none of the guys in this book are any good, either, but the female characters are prominent, and <b>I hate the female hate in this book.</b><br><br>Gemma is a bitch. She doesn't deserve the angelic Ben. <blockquote>
  <i>Gemma is a vindictive, selfish, spoiled girl who doesn’t deserve Ariel and certainly doesn’t deserve Ben’s love.</i>
</blockquote>Every attempt is made in this book to paint Gemma in a bad light, including making her the beautiful outcast rich girl, to making her <b>a slutty character</b> who plays around with boys like they were toys (and therefore deserves her heartbreak).<br><br><u>Ben! The Abusive Romantic!</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>“He was only protecting her.”<br>“Like he was protecting you today?”<br>“Ye-es.” Something in her voice makes me certain my answer won’t satisfy her.<br>“Ariel … violent people usually have a good excuse for why they’re violent. But even a good excuse is just an excuse.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Oh, I'm sorry, did I accidentally read a New Adult novel?</b> Ben is violent. He's beaten up people before. He's gotten arrested for it. But it's ok, because Ben was doing it for the sake of other people. He only beats up the bad guys ~_~ Therefore his violence is TOTALLY justified.<br><br>Ben flirts with Juliet/Ariel while dating her best friend.<blockquote>
  <i>I would almost swear that Ben is flirting. With me. Right in front of his soul mate. Which is so bad that bad can’t even begin to describe it.</i>
</blockquote>Uh, yah, you took the words right out of my mouth.<br><br>Ben, who speaks with the eloquence of a thousand John Mayers.<blockquote>
  <i>“I know you,” he says, with a quiet assurance that threatens to make my tears start all over again. “I know you’re strong and as beautiful on the inside as you are on the outside. I know you like to eat and hate Shakespeare—at least the love stories—and would do anything for a friend. I know you’re an artist, and you made a wall of bricks look like it should be hanging in a museum."</i>
</blockquote><b>Ben, who is Mexican.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Olvida la escuela,” he says, anger in his eyes.</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7361380658647467378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191344996?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191344996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6139653922976358872">FINAL RATING: 1.25 STARS<br/><br/><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br/>I wanted to like this book. I really did. It was one of those books I heard about by random chance and immediately started counting down the days to its release. It looked that good, and was beautiful besides. And when I finally bought it, with its gorgeous cover, I was ecstatic. I dove right in. The beginning was amazing and drew me in right away. And now? I'm embarrassed to admit I own it. Yet another time where I've let beautifully written dust jacket blurb</span>
  <span id="freeText6139653922976358872" style="display:none">FINAL RATING: 1.25 STARS<br /><br /><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br />I wanted to like this book. I really did. It was one of those books I heard about by random chance and immediately started counting down the days to its release. It looked that good, and was beautiful besides. And when I finally bought it, with its gorgeous cover, I was ecstatic. I dove right in. The beginning was amazing and drew me in right away. And now? I'm embarrassed to admit I own it. Yet another time where I've let beautifully written dust jacket blurbs and lovely covers suck me in.<br /><br />This review will contain <b>spoilers</b>. Major ones. And profanity, so if that insults you, stop here. Please. <i>However, my clean, profanity-free review can be found on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com/2011/11/juliet-immortal-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>.</i><br /><br />Seriously. There is <b>A LOT</b> of profanity. I'm not sure I've ever used so much in a review before. Or at all, for that matter.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br />Was I supposed to like her at all? Juliet was vapid, shallow, and selfish. Not to mention that she could never stick to a decision. Ever. All she ever did was complain about how she hates Romeo because he killed her, and then near the end of the book she remembers that <b>SHE FUCKING KILLED HERSELF</b>. What. The. Fuck?!? There are no words sufficient to describe the stupidity of this!! "Oops. My bad! You didn't kill me. So I've been hating you all these years for nothing! Shit!" It makes no sense!! Basically, she's wasted her entire centuries of her life. And what was with the whole "I hated myself but I should really love myself" shit? It sounded too thrown in at the last moment, too rushed. There was no real substance and throughout the entire book Juliet felt so false and fake.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LOVE INTEREST</u>
</b><br />Um. So. What about him? Let's see, he's hot, he's dreamy, he's hot, he's dreamy, and, oh yeah, in his past life he was <b>BENVOLIO FUCKING MONTAGUE</b>. This makes absolutely no sense and felt so thrown in! Can you say <i>random</i>? Or how about <i>I have no clue what to write so I think I'll throw this in</i>? It felt like Jay needed to end the book so she made something up at the last minute. Too bad it makes no sense. And what was with his creepy, overprotectiveness? Not to mention his weird, annoying habit of being stupid and obtuse? He annoyed the hell out of me! Where's the good character traits that I'm supposed to fall in love with?! Why was he so shallow? Why does Juliet love him? Answers, please!! There's not even anything good to say about him. He talks too much and when he talks nothing that makes even remote sense comes out of his mouth.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE VILLAIN</u>
</b><br />Romeo is the only remotely interesting character in this book. He has a sexy, bad boy attitude that's actually attractive. He's supposed to be evil, at least according to Juliet, but I don't see it. I love the two or three intermezzos (incidentally, I speak Italian. <i>Intermezzo</i> means interval. Which makes no sense. Just saying) when we get to hear the story from his point of view. He has a gorgeous, sarcastic voice and his parts are actually well written.He has more depth than every other character combined. he has regrets, and he made his choices. he has to live by them, but he doesn't have to like them. I love that about him and I wish there were more characters like him in this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE "BEST FRIEND"</u>
</b><br />Ariel's best friend, Gemma, is so freaking annoying. Talk about a spoiled brat. Although Juliet couldn't seem to make up her mind about her, liking her one moment and hating her the next. So bipolar!! Make up your damn mind. There's not much to say about her, but I wanted to say this, so here goes: what was the point of her, exactly?<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br />The plot was, like, OMG, <i>amazing</i>.<br /><br />Wait, that's not right. It sucked.<br /><br />Juliet is so freaking indecisive, which does not help the plot at all.<br /><br />I must be with Ben. I love him.<br />I can't be with Ben. He's supposed to love Gemma.<br />Screw Gemma! Ben, let's make out.<br />Go away, Ben! We can't ever be together!<br />Actually, let's elope.<br /><br />Or try this one:<br /><br />Romeo, I'm not working with you.<br />Oh, Romeo, fine. Let's get it over with.<br />Just kidding. I want to stay with Ben.<br />No! Wait! I need your help!<br />Screw you. I don't want to speak to you again.<br /><br />And so on and so forth. So the book drags on for pages and pages of unnecessary shit where nothing happens.<br /><br />Basically, Juliet makes out with Romeo to convince Ben that they're together so he and Gemma can be together. Then she realizes Gemma and Mike are soul mates and Ben is <i>her</i> soul mate. They make out and fall in love. A bit too convenient, don't you think?<br /><br />Hmm, you're right. <i>Way</i> too convenient.<br /><br />And what happens? Love. Yep. That pretty much sums up the whole plot. So let's move on…<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br />Romeo and Juliet fall in love in about five days, give or take. The author says she doesn't believe this love was real, and yet she has Ben and Juliet fall in love in three days? It makes no fucking sense. There's no substance to the romance. Seriously, if anyone knows why Ben and Juliet fall in love, please tell me. Because it looks like a serious fucking case of insta-love to me. All they ever do is make out. They never actually have a deep conversation. And let's not mention that Juliet is technically lying to him about who she is. So he's in love with a stranger and doesn't know it. Lovely. How wonderful for them that they can fall in love without knowing one another <i>at all</i>. It seems to me like Juliet is repeating her mistake. How great. What a wonderful message to send to the world.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING</u>
</b><br />Oh my God. ALTERNATE UNIVERSES. <i>Are you fucking kidding me?</i> This feels so thrown in at the last second! Innocent Ariel is lying on the ground. She's going to die, and so is Juliet. <i>But wait!</i> Juliet gets sent to an alternate universe! And Ariel exists in a another universe too, so it's okay! Well, what about <i>this</i> universe?!? I hate this. The damn alternate universe thing is such a damn crutch. Jay is basically saying she had no clue as to how to end the book, so she threw in alternate universes. Where Juliet falls in love with Ben as Benvolio Montague, in her original body. Instantly. And everything is happy and cheerful. Except for the fact that it's completely unbelievable. She gets a new life in the most pathetic way possible. And Ariel can start over. But since she, you know, <i>died</i> in this universe, making everything that Juliet was semi-decent enough to try to do for her, completely fucking pointless! Because she's <i>dead</i>! So the entire book was a waste!! Why not just start at the fucking ending?!? She might as well have!! Everything that happens throughout the entire book becomes irrelevant at the end. Ariel starts out in a new universe as Romeo's second chance. Great! So clean! Except for the major plot hole: where did the fucking alternate universes come from?! And why are the Ambassadors the only one who can use them?! Oh, and what happened to the Mercenaries?! Never mind them! We got our happy ending! Yeah. <i>Sure</i>.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br />Juliet is the narrator. 'Nuff said.<br />No, but seriously, her voice is so annoying. I might've actually enjoyed the book more told from third person P.O.V. or someone else's P.O.V. Romeo's brief chapters, for example, I actually enjoyed. He has a dark, sardonic voice that pulls you in. Juliet, on the other hand, pushes your away. There's really not much else to say. Juliet was irritating and Romeo was not.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>WRAPUP</u>
</b><br />Will I read the sequel? Probably only if it's about Romeo. And even then, only if it has a nice cover. Otherwise, I'd be too ashamed to buy it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>A SPECIAL NOTE ON THE QUOTE ON THE BACK OF THE DUST JACKET ON THE HARDCOVER U.S. EDITION</u>
</b><br />That was a mouthful. Anyway, that seemingly romantic quote on the back of the book? Well, not only does it turn out it would've sounded stupid because there was no love between Ben and Juliet that I could see, she doesn't even say it. She just thinks it. How lame is that? Pathetic, I know.<br /><br />FINE.<br /><br />Find this review and more on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com/2011/11/juliet-immortal-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6139653922976358872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196590542" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196590542?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196590542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12016023129628376998"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Interesting beginning... middle had highs and lows... ending was PERFECT...</b><br/><br/>I appreciate that not everyone is going to like this book. It's very much a Marmite kind of thing - you either love it or you hate it - except, unlike Marmite, I loved it! I think I liked it even more because it was very far from what I was expecting... and I had expected all kinds of possible ways this could go: super luvvy-duvvy romance, melodrama, ultra-angst...<br/><br/>Okay, there was the teensiest, tiniest bit of teen ang</span>
  <span id="freeText12016023129628376998" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Interesting beginning... middle had highs and lows... ending was PERFECT...</b><br><br>I appreciate that not everyone is going to like this book. It's very much a Marmite kind of thing - you either love it or you hate it - except, unlike Marmite, I loved it! I think I liked it even more because it was very far from what I was expecting... and I had expected all kinds of possible ways this could go: super luvvy-duvvy romance, melodrama, ultra-angst...<br><br>Okay, there was the teensiest, tiniest bit of teen angst but I thought it all worked, it wasn't too much and the words were oh so pretty! I must stress this, I thought the writing was beautiful in that I-must-quote-this kind of way but you find it hard to choose which bit to quote. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> but not <i>that</i> good.<br><br>I read it mainly because I am obsessed with Shakespeare. I went through High School with this ancient but really cool English teacher who taught me how awesome Shakespeare is and was entirely responsible for my good grades in the subject. Now I find myself exasperated and reading the same old takes on Shakespeare's work; Romeo and Juliet must have been re-written into every culture and time period possible by now. But this. Well, this was different. Suddenly, it isn't a tale about the famous star-crossed lovers who sacrificed everything for love. <br><br>Oh no. Because the tagline says it all: <i>"The greatest love story ever told is a lie..."</i><br><br>That's right. Romeo is not what we all thought he was... he's a manipulative SOB who betrayed Juliet and over the centuries the two have battled it out against one another, fighting for control of the destinies of soulmates. Sound a bit TRUE-WUV-y?? It isn't. Or I didn't think so. I thought it was nasty and gruesome and really interesting.<br><br>And the ending was wonderful. You know, I had the smallest recollection of something in the back of my mind early on that led me to suspect something that I quickly disregarded. But I was right. Certain things are not coincidences and there's more to this story than first meets the eye... excited yet? You should be.<br><br>Also, you should know, even though the novel has no sex, there's some not-so-subtle innuendos and girly 'tingling'. Excellent!<br><br></span>

<div id="review_159941945" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159941945" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285872916p2/2276205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159941945?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159941945" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4355034052749861239"><i>Juliet Immortal</i> was one of my most anticipated books of 2011. I loved Stacey Jay’s <i>Dead on the Delta</i>, and when I learned that she was writing a Shakespeare spin-off involving an original type of paranormal being, it seemed like too much awesomeness in one package. I really wanted to like <i>Juliet Immortal</i>, and it makes me sad that I did not.<br/><br/>Here’s the premise: Romeo and Juliet fell in love in medieval Italy, but their story ended rather differently than the version we all know. Romeo sacrificed Ju</span>
  <span id="freeText4355034052749861239" style="display:none"><i>Juliet Immortal</i> was one of my most anticipated books of 2011. I loved Stacey Jay’s <i>Dead on the Delta</i>, and when I learned that she was writing a Shakespeare spin-off involving an original type of paranormal being, it seemed like too much awesomeness in one package. I really wanted to like <i>Juliet Immortal</i>, and it makes me sad that I did not.<br /><br />Here’s the premise: Romeo and Juliet fell in love in medieval Italy, but their story ended rather differently than the version we all know. Romeo sacrificed Juliet to gain eternal life in a supernatural faction called the Mercenaries. When Juliet died, her soul was claimed by the Mercenaries’ rivals, the Ambassadors. The Ambassadors’ goal is to make sure soul-mate couples get together and commit to each other. The Mercenaries’ goal is to destroy these couples by getting one of the lovers to sacrifice the other, as Romeo did to Juliet. Ambassadors possess the bodies of living people while carrying out their missions. Mercenaries can only possess the bodies of the dead.<br /><br />As <i>Juliet Immortal</i> begins, Juliet is sent into the body of Ariel Dragland, an insecure teenage girl who is beautiful but can’t see it because of a burn scar on her face. Juliet, while in Ariel’s body, begins to fall in love again for the first time in 700 years, with a classmate named Ben. Trouble is, Ben is one of the soul mates she’s supposed to be helping, and his counterpart is Ariel’s best friend Gemma. Yet Ben and Gemma barely seem to like each other, and between that and Juliet’s growing feelings, she has a difficult task ahead of her. Meanwhile, Romeo is being creepy as usual, but has some troubling information to impart about the Ambassadors and the Mercenaries.<br /><br />There are scenes in <i>Juliet Immortal</i> that are absolute gems. Juliet’s heart-to-heart conversation with Ariel’s mother is one of them, as is the scene in which Juliet forgives herself for the events of long ago. These scenes reminded me why I like Jay’s writing in the first place, and made me wish even more fervently that I could like the book.<br /><br />Unfortunately, it bogs down in Juliet’s angst, which is fueled by her missing something that’s obvious to the reader long before Juliet figures it out. (Edited to add: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's not obvious <i>who</i> Gemma's real soul mate is, but it's obvious it's not Ben and that there are actually two pairs running around. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>)There’s a contrived reason that the biggest piece of evidence is not visible to her, but there are enough other clues that she should have at least considered the possibility that all was not as it seemed. I wanted to shout at her through the pages to stop brooding and <i>think</i> for a minute.<br /><br />Then, in the later chapters, the metaphysics and the backstory become confusing. Bombshells are dropped regarding the common roots of the Ambassadors and Mercenaries, the real nature of Romeo’s character and of his dastardly deed, where Juliet’s mentor is hiding and what she’s really up to, and alternate universes. Yet none of this is explored or explained as much as it could have been.<br /><br />The ending added to my frustration. MAJOR SPOILERS: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tragedy strikes, but then both Juliet and Romeo are whisked away into hopeful alternate-universe endings. I felt that I was supposed to be happy for them, but instead I couldn’t escape the thought that in “real” reality, the reality in which most of the book was set, everyone’s lives had just been shattered. About half the main characters were dead and the other half devastated, and all to save a “soul mate” relationship that contains a troubling power imbalance. (I AM NOT UNBIASED. I'm the product of a teacher/student relationship. I wouldn't be here without it, but it was a seriously messed up marriage.) I think I’d have preferred either the sad ending alone, or a happy ending in the “main” reality. However, I did like Juliet’s alternate ending taken in isolation, and would have loved to read a straight 14th-century retelling that ended like that.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Stacey Jay is a good writer and I’m not giving up on her. I’ll definitely keep following her Annabelle Lee books. <i>Juliet Immortal</i>, though, left me more frustrated than satisfied, and I can’t really recommend it despite its originality and some terrific scenes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4355034052749861239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_203550347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203550347" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203550347?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=girls-who-do-things">girls-who-do-things</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=good-uns">good-uns</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203550347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1223139309909644377">Originally published <a href='http://angieville.blogspot.com/2011/08/juliet-immortal-by-stacey-jay.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a>.<br/><br/>What a beautiful cover. I remember when I first saw it my initial thought was, <i>Oh, please don't let it suck</i>. I know that sounds harsh, but sometimes a cover just calls out to you and you know when you finally hold a physical copy of the book itself you'll just want to stroke it and love it and tell it it's found its home on your shelves. Unfortunately, the innards (as my boy is fond of saying) don't always match the outtards. And then I am forced to cry. Because . . . s</span>
  <span id="freeText1223139309909644377" style="display:none">Originally published <a href="http://angieville.blogspot.com/2011/08/juliet-immortal-by-stacey-jay.html" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />What a beautiful cover. I remember when I first saw it my initial thought was, <i>Oh, please don't let it suck</i>. I know that sounds harsh, but sometimes a cover just calls out to you and you know when you finally hold a physical copy of the book itself you'll just want to stroke it and love it and tell it it's found its home on your shelves. Unfortunately, the innards (as my boy is fond of saying) don't always match the outtards. And then I am forced to cry. Because . . . so pretty. So when a review copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1691206.Stacey_Jay" title="Stacey Jay" rel="nofollow noopener">Stacey Jay</a>'s JULIET IMMORTAL came my way, I held my breath. Just a bit. Okay, maybe for the first five pages or so. Thankfully, that's all it took. Because this innovative retelling (of sorts) of Shakespeare's <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> has teeth. And they sank into me with delicious ferocity. This was my first foray with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1691206.Stacey_Jay" title="Stacey Jay" rel="nofollow noopener">Stacey Jay</a>, though I know she has a handful of books already out. After this encounter, I look forward to checking out her other work.<br /><br />Juliet Capulet's nightmare is never going to end. No one knows what really happened to her. Murdered by her true love, Juliet is saved at the last minute by powerful but nebulous forces of good (known as the Ambassadors), who recruit her immortal soul in their timeless battle against the powers of evil (known as the Mercenaries). Filled with grief and hate at Romeo's unforgivable action, Juliet accepts the offer and finds herself pitted against Romeo, who essentially sold his soul to the Mercs for promised immortality. And the two of them face one another over and over and over again. For seven hundred years, they've been racing against the clock and each other to save (in Juliet's case) or damn (in Romeo's) pairs of soul mates, literally slipping into human bodies (in Juliet's case) and dead ones (in Romeo's) in order to sway their charges for good or ill. Each and every time Romeo tries to kill Juliet and Juliet fights back and escapes, though she is forbidden from taking his life as part of her mission for the Ambassadors. But this time--this mission--something is different. And they can both tell. This time more seems to be riding on the outcome than just a point scored for one side or the other. This time it's difficult to tell just who exactly are the soul mates, just who loves who. This time Juliet may not escape with her immortal soul intact.<br /><br />JULIET IMMORTAL wins because it is both a competent retelling and re-envisioning of the most famous star-crossed lovers of all time, while managing not to forget the ruthlessness, violence, and eerie inevitability of the original. In fact, I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1691206.Stacey_Jay" title="Stacey Jay" rel="nofollow noopener">Stacey Jay</a>'s clever explanations went a long way toward fleshing out the characters and events of the play. I certainly loved the life and depth she breathed into both leads. How brave Juliet is. And evil Romeo? Where have you been all my life? There are no ifs, ands, or buts about it. This Romeo is evil, he's out for Juliet's blood, and the enmity between them is real. The story starts off with a bang, literally, as Juliet is flung into the body of a girl who has just decided to end it all and drive the car she's in off a cliff, taking her shoddy date with her. It's one of my favorite scenes in the book and the first one to give me real chills. Right after the crash (taken from my uncorrected ARC):<br /><blockquote>Dylan's eyes flutter open.<br /><br />Even in the moonlight shining through the ceiling they look dark, peculiar. There's something strange about this boy, something warped inside him. I'm not surprised that he played a cruel trick on Ariel, but I'm curious to see what he'll do next. How will he deal with the fact that she nearly killed them both?<br /><br />"Ariel?" he asks, his voice slurred. "Are you okay?"<br /><br />"Ye-yes, I think so." Maybe he doesn't remember how the car crashed? If so, I won't be helping him with his recall. I keep my expression carefully blank. "Are you okay?"<br /><br />"I think I'm fine. I . . . think I might be . . ." His words fade as he leans closer. He's staring at me. I can feel it, though his chin is tipped down, creating hollows the light through the roof can't touch.<br /><br />The roof! I look up, and a sigh of relief escapes my lips. Glass. It's made of glass! Thank goodness. Getting out of this car seems like a better idea with every passing second. If Dylan is this disturbing at eighteen, he'll be a serial killer by the time he's twenty.<br /><br />"We'll be fine. We just need to get out." I lift blood-slicked fingers to pry at the latch, ignoring Dylan when he leans even closer.<br /><br />The sunroof is manually operated. I see that the glass panel can pop out, but the mechanism gives me a bit of trouble. Still, I'll get it open and there will be plenty of room for us to fit through the hole. Me first, of course.<br /><br />"I'm sorry, could I--" He exhales, his breath hot on my neck. I fight the urge to shudder. "Could I ask you something?"<br /><br />He wants to talk. Lovely.<br /><br />I sigh. "Sure." I pull on the hinges, then realize I should have been pushing and sigh again.<br /><br />"Has anyone told you your hair looks silver in the moonlight?"<br /><br />I glance in the rearview mirror. My new hair does look silver, like something from a fairy tale. And the rest of what I can see of myself is equally haunting--shocking, really.<br /><br />Why does Ariel think herself so repulsive? Huge blue eyes dominate my new face, dwarfing my small nose and thin lips. The scars on my cheek and jaw are visible, but they aren't as terrible as Ariel thinks. The face looking back at me is attractive, compelling. There's something about it that makes you want to look twice.<br /><br />So I do, staring a little too long, giving myself away.<br /><br />Dylan laughs, his lips suddenly far too close to mine. "But soft, what light through yonder window breaks?"<br /><br />No. It can't be. We've never-- <i>He's</i> never--<br /><br />"Did you miss me, love?" He kisses me on the cheek, a rough, playful kiss that leaves a bit of wet behind.<br /><br />Dylan has died after all. And Romeo has found a corpse. It's my last thought before his hands are around my throat.</blockquote><br />Yep. Chills. There's also a pretty sweet love story going on within the pages. I was delighted with who <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1691206.Stacey_Jay" title="Stacey Jay" rel="nofollow noopener">Stacey Jay</a> chose for Juliet and how she updated him for a contemporary take. Their initial encounter is another of my very favorite scenes in the book, and my affection for them lasted for the duration the story. So much so that I actually could have done with a little more connection between the modern boy and the one from the play as it would have enriched the bond for me. That part, along with one section in which Juliet sort of uncharacteristically fails to make a few connections, are the only instances that bothered me a bit. Otherwise, the novel's strengths stood out, particularly older-and-wise Juliet herself. She's such a strong character, able to contain a plethora of rich and complex emotions. She is clawing her way toward revenge or peace, whichever comes first. I loved her fire, and I loved how the writing reflected her rage and pain, without marring that original, first love between the two kids from Verona. Rather, it supports its authenticity in all its breathless perfection. Which then only highlights the atrocious betrayal and the loss she feels. It's all very affecting and enjoyable. As is Juliet's foray in young Ariel's body. Her interactions with Ariel's well-nigh estranged mother and her problematic best friend Gemma are nuanced and gripping. Lastly, I do have to say that my favorite thing about this book is that it scared me. There are a couple of scenes in particular that gave me the cold shivers, and I just love it when that happens. All in all, JULIET IMMORTAL is an unexpectedly visceral read. I thoroughly enjoyed it and look forward to handing it around.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1223139309909644377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_213804499" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213804499" />
    <a title="Parvathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy"><img alt="Parvathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425840439p2/4915009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/213804499?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parvathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parvathy" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy">Parvathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like contemporary takes on well  known stories, YA readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Parvathy by: </span>
      goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=movie-material">movie-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=glued-till-the-last-page">glued-till-the-last-page</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=romeos-and-juliets">romeos-and-juliets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=feel-good">feel-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer213804499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8580786431453992490">This is not your typical Romeo and Juliet love story. For one thing the starting premise is the one where Juliet did not commit suicide for the sake of everlasting true love as the Bard's version claims but was killed by her lover Romeo who exchanged her life for immortality. But the betrayed and forsaken Juliet did not die according to plan. On the contrary she become an immortal, an ambassador of light whose sole purpose is fight for the sake of true loves across time against her one true love</span>
  <span id="freeText8580786431453992490" style="display:none">This is not your typical Romeo and Juliet love story. For one thing the starting premise is the one where Juliet did not commit suicide for the sake of everlasting true love as the Bard's version claims but was killed by her lover Romeo who exchanged her life for immortality. But the betrayed and forsaken Juliet did not die according to plan. On the contrary she become an immortal, an ambassador of light whose sole purpose is fight for the sake of true loves across time against her one true love and arch nemesis Romeo. Reborn in to the mortal realm each time soul mates find each other Juliet has to give up the life she inhabits each time her job is completed. But the irony of the matter is Juliet who is destined to bring true loves together herself do not believe in true love. After her experience with true love Juliet wants nothing more to do with it herself. But that is until she meets Ben a kind hearted boy with whom she experiences an instant connection. Now when circumstances urges Juliet to rethink her position Romeo enters the picture and he will do anything to ensure that Juliet remains his for all eternity. <br /><br />When I first picked up this book I admit I wasn't much excited to read about a YA Romeo and Juliet story. In fact that was the last thing I wanted. But my inquisitiveness got the best of me and I decided to give it a try. Surprisingly I found this book a very enjoyable and interesting read. The concept is fresh and the treatment commendable. The one part worth mentioning is the practicality associated with the story of Romeo and Juliet. Rather than portraying Romeo and Juliet as the symbols of undying love the book makes you think about practical scenarios looking at Romeo as an exiled 17 year old noble with no skill or livelihood and Juliet as a 14 year old innocent girl who never had to face actual hardship in her well pampered life. The book portrays Juliet as a strong and stubborn character who has faced her share of challenges but still moves forward strongly, Romeo as a misunderstood and naive character who is forced to live with the consequences of his wrong choices. Even though Romeo was portrayed as an evil character I couldn't find it in me to hate him. The new character Ben on the other hand is likable and refreshing. It is always a treat to read about characters who are so sure of what they want and do not shy away from expressing it. The premise and settings are well developed and the story manages to engage you in all the crucial points. This book I would recommend to all those readers who are willing to keep and open mind and treat the story from an entirely different point of view. Some readers though may find it difficult to cope with some of the liberties the author has taken with the Romeo and Juliet story but here also open mindedness is the key. But this book like most books is not without its own set of flaws that stick out. For one thing it goes on and on about the concept of love. But if you are willing to overlook such misgivings you might find your self highly satisfied. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8580786431453992490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_193030156" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193030156" />
    <a title="Kt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3681846-kt"><img alt="Kt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599666402p2/3681846.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193030156?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kt" href="/user/show/3681846-kt">Kt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3681846-kt?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193030156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2571218523709942966">Forget everything you thought to be true about Romeo and Juliet's story. It isn't some great tragedy with starcrossed lovers that couldn't bear to be apart. No, it's a story about betrayal. Romeo murdered Juliet in hopes for his own immortality, but in a twist of fate, Juliet was granted the same. Only, she serves on the side of light, whose job it is to protect true lovers from people like Romeo who would tear it all apart. It's been over 700 years of fighting him and his kind every step of the</span>
  <span id="freeText2571218523709942966" style="display:none">Forget everything you thought to be true about Romeo and Juliet's story. It isn't some great tragedy with starcrossed lovers that couldn't bear to be apart. No, it's a story about betrayal. Romeo murdered Juliet in hopes for his own immortality, but in a twist of fate, Juliet was granted the same. Only, she serves on the side of light, whose job it is to protect true lovers from people like Romeo who would tear it all apart. It's been over 700 years of fighting him and his kind every step of the way. All that changes when Juliet starts to fall in love again. It's a forbidden love, and we all know just how Romeo feels about that. Juliet may just lose love again, after it's taken her so long to finally believe again, and then nothing will be able to save her broken heart.<br /><br />Juliet is truly broken for lack of a better word. She doesn't realize this, but in her quests to ensure couples find their soul mates, her heart just in the task. Yes, she thinks everyone deserves love, but in the end she's really only going through the motions rather than believing in love anymore. In fact Juliet is filled with more anger and hate towards Romeo and her situation to really be able to believe in much of anything. I think this is what made her slow opening of her heart again all the more sweet. Granted the love did seem to come about with nothing to really establish it, but then they do say love at first sight can be real, and this book makes a very good case for it.<br /><br />I had assumed I would hate Romeo's character based on the description, and in the beginning, I did. However, the more I got to see him, the more I realized that there was so much more than met the eyes. I had thought he was an evil uncaring character, but I couldn't have been wrong. He truly is a tortured soul who has had to live with his mistakes for a very long time. To be honest, I'm not really sure the punishment fits the crime, as in the end he really was only weak rather than evil. Of course that punishment has had such a long time to fester, making him now capable of terrible things. Even though he appears to live to torment, you can see that he hates it all, making me wonder if somehow there is some goodness left deep down inside of him.<br /><br />To be honest, I never really cared for Romeo and Juliet's story. I just hated the tragedy of it. I just think for something to be considered a great love story, then there should be some happiness there, which we all know just isn't the case. I just found the whole sacrifice thing to be quite sickening to be honest. Love should go on, no matter what. So, when I read the description of this book, I was very excited. I couldn't wait to read something that would turn the original story upside down, and Juliet Immortal definitely did not disappoint in that area. From the moment I picked Juliet Immortal up, I just could not put it down. So if you are like me and would love to see the "greatest" tragedy of all times get a little shake up, or even if you just enjoy reading about second chances at love, then Juliet Immortal is one book you won't want to miss. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2571218523709942966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156306317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156306317" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156306317?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156306317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer462142955071272824">"Romeo, Romeo, where art thou Romeo?"<br/>"Why, right here, my love!"<br/>"Oh Romeo, whyfore dost thou kiss me so?"<br/>"All the better to suck your soul away, my love."<br/><br/>I couldn't resist, okay! And I know Shakespeare is turning over in his grave (I feel obliged to apologise to Krystle too) but people, Romeo and Juliet! In a YA novel set in contemporary times. How awesome is that? And Romeo and Juliet on opposite side of the spectrum with Romeo batting for the bad guys! Even more awesome. But (and Shakespeare c</span>
  <span id="freeText462142955071272824" style="display:none">"Romeo, Romeo, where art thou Romeo?"<br />"Why, right here, my love!"<br />"Oh Romeo, whyfore dost thou kiss me so?"<br />"All the better to suck your soul away, my love."<br /><br />I couldn't resist, okay! And I know Shakespeare is turning over in his grave (I feel obliged to apologise to Krystle too) but people, Romeo and Juliet! In a YA novel set in contemporary times. How awesome is that? And Romeo and Juliet on opposite side of the spectrum with Romeo batting for the bad guys! Even more awesome. But (and Shakespeare certainly did roll over for this one) Romeo and Juliet are out to annihilate each other. (You can't kill someone who's already dead. You have to annihilate them.) So yes, fantastic premise. I couldn't wait to sink my teeth into it and examine it in great detail and with great delight.<br /><br />And I liked it. I did. It was very readable and there was only one thing that jumped out at me (which took away two stars) but honestly? As far as entertainment goes, it was very entertaining. Juliet has a strong, clean voice and I appreciated that she made time to work out her body's Mommy issues - and wow, yeah, body, host, you get the idea, right? I liked the atmosphere set, the absolutely chilling feeling that accompanies you when you see a ghost of yourself. Jay does this is all very well and I liked that she did it all very well. The mean girl trope sort of goes through a metamorphosis and changes in ways I'm not sure I approve of but apart from an occasional mutter about the stupidity of it all, it's not as offensive as it has the potential to be. And this is totally girly of me but the love interest? Totally swoon-inducing. At least to me. I thought he was hotness personified which might, in some way, explain this rambling thing that I'm trying to pass off as a review.<br /><br />But. And you ought to have known it was coming. <br /><br />The thing that detracted from the novel in a big way, in my opinion solely, is the deus ex machina (which, if you are like I was and clueless about what deus ex machina is, Wikipedia provides a definition: <i>is a plot device whereby a seemingly inextricable problem is suddenly and abruptly solved with the contrived and unexpected intervention of some new event, character, ability, or object</i>). The ending seemed too abrupt, too neat and way too contrived to be satisfying in any degree. It felt forced. I didn't like that. I really didn't. I mean, you go through the book trying to make your brain forget the fact that Juliet is, you know, 14 in a 16 year old's body but mentally more than a 100, wow, it gets convoluted but you make your Brain ignore that and then, the ending. And you are like...<br /><br />Oh no... what? Where? How? WHY? (It's not a sad ending though.)<br /><br />However, it seems that Romeo gets to have his own story so we should look forward to that. Well, I am anyway. Looking forward to it, I mean.</span>
  <a data-text-id="462142955071272824" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_196197221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196197221" />
    <a title="Eve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/758088-eve"><img alt="Eve" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491192188p2/758088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196197221?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eve" href="/user/show/758088-eve">Eve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196197221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4501945258360972704">Upon hearing about Juliet Immortal by Stacey Jay- which turns the famous tragic love story on its ear – I was immediately desirous of it. I relished the notion of a kickass Juliet protecting true lovers and battling, rather than mooning over, an evil Romeo. I thought Juliet Immortal would be the novel for all those who had ever sacrificed everything for love only to find out they’ve been cruelly played. Can you tell I’m building up to a “but?” <br/><br/>Juliet Immortal strove for that to some extent BUT f</span>
  <span id="freeText4501945258360972704" style="display:none">Upon hearing about Juliet Immortal by Stacey Jay- which turns the famous tragic love story on its ear – I was immediately desirous of it. I relished the notion of a kickass Juliet protecting true lovers and battling, rather than mooning over, an evil Romeo. I thought Juliet Immortal would be the novel for all those who had ever sacrificed everything for love only to find out they’ve been cruelly played. Can you tell I’m building up to a “but?” <br /><br />Juliet Immortal strove for that to some extent BUT fell short of my very hopeful expectations. <br /><br />I have never been a huge fan of the play. As my son said, it’s “kinda stupid” to kill yourself over someone else. “It’s all that friar’s fault,” he added. I agree. <br /><br />And yet Shakespeare’s Romeo and Juliet have been the poster couple for ideal, romantic love for centuries. <br /><br /><i>"'O, she doth teach the torches to burn bright,' he whispers...<br /><br />"That horrible play. That contemptible, lying play he helped Shakespeare pen all those hundreds of years ago when he first twisted our story to fit his agenda. It worked far too well. Shakespeare's enduring tragedy did its part to further the goals of the Mercenaries---glamorizing death, making dying for love seem the most noble act of all, though nothing could be further from the truth. Taking an innocent life---in a misguided attempt to prove love or for any other reason---is a useless waste."</i><br /><br />Amen, sister! The Juliet of Juliet Immortal is full of anger, still punishing herself for loving a faithless Romeo. Who among us hasn’t fallen for the wrong guy – handsome, persuasive with false sincerity, full of poetic promises of forever? Only in Juliet’s case, the wrong guy got her to kill herself to secure his own eternal life. <br /><br />Upon her death, Juliet was given a choice by an Ambassador of Light – to fight for their cause, which is to make sure that soulmates on earth come and remain together. Juliet commits herself to waking up every 50 or so years in someone else’s body and assuming her life, in order to protect true lovers. However, working against the Ambassadors of Light and soulmates are the Mercenaries. On their side is the dastardly Romeo, who continues to live – but only if he furthers the Mercenaries’ mission, which is to keep true lovers apart. <br /><br />The setup is fantastic and our heroine and villain have dynamic scenes that crackle with electricity. Juliet is driven and fiesty, but not so bitter that she doesn’t believe in true love. After all, her sole purpose in the afterlife is to be a sort of avenging angel of lovers. And although strong, she is also portrayed as too self-sacrificing, a flaw which the author spotlights. It is both a comment on the original Juliet and a mirror to suggestive young girls who fall in love too hard, too fast for the first time. <br /><br />Despite his evil ways, Romeo, like all seductive players, has the charming narcissism that leaves no doubt as to why Juliet fell for him in the first place. By the end of the book, my hatred for him in the beginning, upon seeing the ugly face behind the beautiful poetry, had changed to pity. I was pleased, though, that the author didn’t turn Juliet into the classic victim/heroine by having her fall back in love with Romeo all over again. In fact, Juliet grows from a place of fury and self-hatred to a more enlightened, even stronger person who thinks for herself rather than blindly loving or blindly following the rules. <br /><br />Another aspect I loved was that Juliet (posing as teenage Ariel) had a parent. That was THERE. You know what I’m talking about, right? Teens in novels with mysteriously absent parents or clueless parents because the authors didn’t know how to write about those pesky parental units. Because in real life, unless you’re an orphan, parents usually get in their children’s business; they rarely stay off scene while their children’s lives are in obvious danger. They usually have at least a clue that something’s up. So thumbs up for Stacey Jay for actually writing about a mother-daughter relationship of depth within this supernatural tale. <br /><br />Juliet’s blind love and self-sacrifice, the mother-daughter relationship, and the defiance of expectations are themes from the original play that are explored with a fresh take in Juliet Immortal. You’ll enjoy this reworking even without having read the play, but even more so if you have, especially with the clever interspersing of the quotes within the narrative, their original meanings seen in a new light. <br /><br />So from where do my misgivings stem? I would think that since Juliet Immortal was set up as as an anithesis to the false love in Shakespeare’s Romeo and Juliet, the love story in it would be more realistic and mature, showing our heroine’s growth. In the play Romeo and Juliet spy each other from across the room and fall in love at first sight. At least Juliet did and look where she ended up. So having learned that hard lesson years ago and being around soulmates for centuries, you would think that when she does fall in love again, it wouldn’t be the insta-love of her youth, right? Wrong. Insta-love part II. <br /><br />The real tragedy is how YA books promote love at first sight as ideal and a surefire, tell-tale sign of true love. Real, true love takes time to build. Trust isn't, shouldn't be, instantaneous. <br /><br />The role of the Ambassadors and Mercenaries confused me. I like the ambiguity of whether they were really good vs. evil or neither and just out for themselves. However, the structure and rules of this universe were puzzling.<br /><br />Finally, the last scene just plain sucked. It was anti-climactic and had none of the beauty of the original play from which the chapter presumably followed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4501945258360972704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
